<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a852f69a-8946-45ce-a8da-08d76aa8c168'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer15842332043579792398"><strong>An extraordinary portrait of true love that will move anyone who has a first love story of their own.</strong> Axi Moore is a "good girl": She studies hard, stays out of the spotlight, and doesn't tell anyone how all she really wants is to run away from it all. The only person she can tell is her best friend, Robinson--who she also happens to be madly in love with. <br/><br/>When Axi spontan</span>
  <span id="freeText15842332043579792398" style="display:none"><strong>An extraordinary portrait of true love that will move anyone who has a first love story of their own.</strong> Axi Moore is a "good girl": She studies hard, stays out of the spotlight, and doesn't tell anyone how all she really wants is to run away from it all. The only person she can tell is her best friend, Robinson--who she also happens to be madly in love with. <br /><br />When Axi spontaneously invites Robinson to come with her on an impulsive cross-country road trip, she breaks the rules for the first time in her life. But the adventure quickly turns from carefree to out of control after the teens find themselves on the run from the police. And when Robinson suddenly collapses, Axi has to face the truth that this trip might be his last.<br /><br />A remarkably moving tale very personal to James Patterson's own past, FIRST LOVE is testament to the power of first love--and how it can change the rest of your life.</span>

<a href="/questions/384805-dear-readers-does-somebody-know-on">Dear readers,

Does somebody know on which page this quote is? I love it, but I somehow cannot find it anymore. I would be really grateful! :)

“I think about what I didn&#39;t say then, which is this: the stars we see aren&#39;t even real stars. We see the light that they gave off millions of years ago but that is only now reaching our eyes. We don&#39;t see a star as much as a memory.”</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/740363247?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah (Head Stuck In A Book)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah (Head Stuck In A Book)" href="/user/show/3116440-sarah-head-stuck-in-a-book">Sarah (Head Stuck In A Book)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316207041" href="/book/show/17899371-first-love">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3116440-sarah-head-stuck-in-a-book?shelf=arc">arc</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer740363247" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3622535795133293974">*SOB* OMG OMG *SOB* OMG!<br/>So I think both Little, Brown and Kleenex need to get together to promote this book, tissues trust me you'll need them!<br/>How can I put into words how brilliant, heart-breaking. emotionally devastating and amazingly fantastic this book is, I can't unless you experience this book for yourselves you just wont understand, it's so much more than those words, the thought that it's based on a real -life story from James Patterson's life makes it even more meaningful and heartfelt.</span>
  <span id="freeText3622535795133293974" style="display:none">*SOB* OMG OMG *SOB* OMG!<br />So I think both Little, Brown and Kleenex need to get together to promote this book, tissues trust me you'll need them!<br />How can I put into words how brilliant, heart-breaking. emotionally devastating and amazingly fantastic this book is, I can't unless you experience this book for yourselves you just wont understand, it's so much more than those words, the thought that it's based on a real -life story from James Patterson's life makes it even more meaningful and heartfelt.<br />Jeez this book made me cry, halfway through is when the tears started, towards the end is when the ugly crying started, and that to me is the work of a fantastic storyteller, one who has you caring about the characters so much that you're left emotionally bereft at the end.<br />I've never read a James Patterson book before, but after reading First Love that is definitely going to change, this book has rocketed up into my list of all-time favorites, a really great contemporary romance based around a road trip with two best friends Axi and Robinson, who will finally admit their feelings for one another in amidst their hijnks during their time on the road, while realising that sometimes life will take a turn that you would never anticipate.<br />I don't want to write too much and give the plot away, but all you contemporary romance fans need to pick this book up, it's amazing, a quick and fast read that's never boring and will keep you glued to the pages up till the very end.<br />Loved it, loved it, loved it!<br />Highly recommended.</span>

<div id="review_856116869" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/856116869" />
    <a title="Jennifer Mahon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4652735-jennifer-mahon"><img alt="Jennifer Mahon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578177091p2/4652735.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/856116869?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Mahon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Mahon" href="/user/show/4652735-jennifer-mahon">Jennifer Mahon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer856116869&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer856116869" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13032729852358643555">***SPOILERS***<br/><br/>Sigh. Seriously, James?? OK, I can almost forgive the complete and total ripoff of Fault in our Stars, as I am sure we will be seeing a lot of those in the upcoming months, but, that aside, the utter implausibility of this book made me slightly insane. <br/><br/>To begin...this entire whirlwind adventure took place in three weeks. The drove from Oregon to California, California to Vegas, Vegas to wherever the hell they were when they stopped in a hospital for a couple of days, hospital to Ne</span>
  <span id="freeText13032729852358643555" style="display:none">***SPOILERS***<br /><br />Sigh. Seriously, James?? OK, I can almost forgive the complete and total ripoff of Fault in our Stars, as I am sure we will be seeing a lot of those in the upcoming months, but, that aside, the utter implausibility of this book made me slightly insane. <br /><br />To begin...this entire whirlwind adventure took place in three weeks. The drove from Oregon to California, California to Vegas, Vegas to wherever the hell they were when they stopped in a hospital for a couple of days, hospital to New York, New York to Philly and, finally, Philly to some undisclosed location in the Carolinas. Right. Three weeks. With plenty of time to stop and camp in the Redwoods, explore Hollywood, hook up with a stripper in Vegas, land in the hospital...you know what, I can't even finish. But, let us not forget that at the end of three weeks...one of them is dead!!! <br /><br />Another rather glaring plot point...holding up a state trooper at gun point?? Roughly two weeks before you are so weak you are dead?? You managed to turn his gun on him and lock him up in his trunk?? I can't.<br /><br />The hospital trip. We are really expected to believe two minors can stroll on into a hospital, one of them clearly dying of cancer and they just take the in, no questions asked. Nobody is worried about insurance, parents, payment. And, clearly, this is the most ridiculous hospital in the worl...since you can just sneak out of ICU without anyone knowing. Fantastic.<br /><br />Then, the 1,440 mile journey in a broken down truck seemed to happen overnight...no need for stops or anything. We just knocked that out in a night. <br /><br />$1500 also managed to cover the cost for this entire trip. Apparently, gas is free in stolen vehicles. Again, fantastic.<br /><br />Then the very dramatic death. It read like a lot of time was passing. Nope, turned out to just be a couple of days. We went from holding up a cop at gun point to death in like 10 days. I get that cancer moves fast, but...seriously?? <br /><br />Then, the brat, I'm sorry...heroine?? Finally returns home and rather nobly turns herself into the police. And then has to go into remedial Physics because skipping three weeks of classes when you are at an AP level apparently just renders you completely stupid. <br /><br />I truly thought this book was just awful. It was hard to root for whatever their names were because they were kind of just spoiled brats. I expect we are meant to feel bad for them since they both had cancer. I'm sorry, but I don't think that excuses a crime spree as they be-bop their way across America. Honestly, I hope she ends up stuck in that town forever. UGH.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13032729852358643555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer827068516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6755605861194808106">Poor attempt at describing a first love. I was really surprised to see the authors glorifying two runaways and stealing a car. Gee, we all had first loves but didn't do things like that. I think Patterson hardly even wrote this book and if he did, I may stop reading him altogether. And to think he co authored this book in memory of his first love who died young. What a shame this was the forum he used to express their time together.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1077376925" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1077376925" />
    <a title="Sharon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11267295-sharon"><img alt="Sharon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546315858p2/11267295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1077376925?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon" href="/user/show/11267295-sharon">Sharon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316207041" href="/book/show/17899371-first-love">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11267295-sharon?shelf=borrowed-from-library">borrowed-from-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1077376925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14266612784053402684">Sixteen year old Axi Moore decided it was time to stop being the good girl and time to live life and go on an adventure. Her best friend Robinson couldn't believe that, Axi was capable of being anything other than a good girl (GG) which he nicknamed her, but he would soon be proven wrong. Together the two of them set off on a road trip where they would discover a world they never knew existed and do things they only dreamed of.<br/><br/>Living life to the fullest and exploring wonderful places along the w</span>
  <span id="freeText14266612784053402684" style="display:none">Sixteen year old Axi Moore decided it was time to stop being the good girl and time to live life and go on an adventure. Her best friend Robinson couldn't believe that, Axi was capable of being anything other than a good girl (GG) which he nicknamed her, but he would soon be proven wrong. Together the two of them set off on a road trip where they would discover a world they never knew existed and do things they only dreamed of.<br /><br />Living life to the fullest and exploring wonderful places along the way, Axi and Robinson couldn't be happier. As days turn into nights it seems, Axi and Robinson have also discovered their feelings towards one another have become more than just friendship. Just as their love for one another begins to blossom their lives take a turn that will bring them back to reality that neither one of them are ready to deal with.<br /><br />This story is so much more than just a love story and one that I thoroughly enjoyed. It will melt heart and will make you laugh, but most of all it will make you remember to enjoy life because life as we know it is very precious. A beautiful story which I have no hesitation in recommending. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14266612784053402684" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14801994584010578463" style="display:none">DNF on Page 55.<br /><br />I borrowed this from the library a while back after seeing Penguin Platform's YouTube channel discuss the book. As someone who loves reading road trip novels, this sounded like my cup of tea. But after starting the book, I was finding the pacing incredibly fast which made the trip a little unrealistic in my view. I put the book down for a while (talking few months) and returned to it recently to see if I could get any further through but again, I struggled and simply concluded that I had lost interest. Overall, I was disappointed.<br /><br />The story followed two characters called Axi and Robinson. Axi had a tough upbringing and she's secretly hidden a crush on Robinson from him for a while. She plans to reveal all on their road trip together. The story follows the road trip and the events that occur including stealing a motorbike. <br /><br />I still love road trip novels though, my reading experience from them wasn't vanished because of this book so if you know any good road trip novels, feel free to recommend some. I read both YA and Adult.</span>

<div id="review_1237937464" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1237937464" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1237937464?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=overdrive-audio">overdrive-audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1237937464" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9755974976969659149">Short yet sweet story about two young people who fall in love despite the challenges they hope to outrun.<br/><br/>I came across <b>First Love</b> and for a couple of reasons it caught my attention. First, I’ve seen it compared to the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars' title='The Fault in Our Stars by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Fault in Our Stars</a> many times and second, there was a road trip in the story. Putting these two elements together, I was sure <b>First Love</b> would capture my interest.<br/><br/>In this novel, Axi Moore and her best friend Robinson decide to throw caution to the wind and take an epic road tri</span>
  <span id="freeText9755974976969659149" style="display:none">Short yet sweet story about two young people who fall in love despite the challenges they hope to outrun.<br /><br />I came across <b>First Love</b> and for a couple of reasons it caught my attention. First, I’ve seen it compared to the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars" title="The Fault in Our Stars by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a> many times and second, there was a road trip in the story. Putting these two elements together, I was sure <b>First Love</b> would capture my interest.<br /><br />In this novel, Axi Moore and her best friend Robinson decide to throw caution to the wind and take an epic road trip while time is still on their side. This decision is huge because everyone knows that Axi is the straight and narrow girl who gets good grades and always does what is expected of her. Her best friend Robinson is the charming boy who can get away with murder and charm the pants off of anyone. <br /><br />As they make their plans and travel from the west to east coast, we get to experience Axi and Robinson’s love unfold along with the reasons that brought them together. <br /><br />There were a few things that seemed a bit choppy with this story. I was surprised the author didn’t bother to make the story more believable when it came to the road trip and Robinson’s condition. I find it hard to believe that two teenagers can do so much in three weeks on such limited funds, as well as committing a few crimes along the way. What also caught me off guard was the sudden and drastic decline of Robinson’s condition. If this novel were a bit longer and better developed, I think their story would have been more plausible and believable.<br /><br />Overall, this was a quick and heartfelt story despite its flaws. I’m always a sucker for dramatic endings and romance, so it wasn’t too bad… just could have been so much better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9755974976969659149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_851581265" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/851581265" />
    <a title="Brenda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2337007-brenda"><img alt="Brenda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577750190p2/2337007.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/851581265?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenda" href="/user/show/2337007-brenda">Brenda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781448108497" href="/book/show/18278113-first-love">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2337007-brenda?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2337007-brenda?shelf=own-read">own-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2337007-brenda?shelf=read-on-kindle">read-on-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2337007-brenda?shelf=2014-release">2014-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2337007-brenda?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2337007-brenda?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2337007-brenda?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer851581265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15686059538788184424">Axi Moore had a big surprise for her best friend. Robinson was one she never seemed to be able to shock, but this time she hoped she could. Cutting classes for the afternoon, she had arranged to meet him at Bernie’s, their favourite hang-out, at 1.30 – when he walked in the door his big smile said it all. But she finally did it – when she told him her plans, and that he was part of it, she waited for his answer; “hell yes” was all the answer she needed.<br/><br/>Axi was GG to Robinson – Good Girl, he call</span>
  <span id="freeText15686059538788184424" style="display:none">Axi Moore had a big surprise for her best friend. Robinson was one she never seemed to be able to shock, but this time she hoped she could. Cutting classes for the afternoon, she had arranged to meet him at Bernie’s, their favourite hang-out, at 1.30 – when he walked in the door his big smile said it all. But she finally did it – when she told him her plans, and that he was part of it, she waited for his answer; “hell yes” was all the answer she needed.<br /><br />Axi was GG to Robinson – Good Girl, he called her. But she wanted to put a dent in that title. With her little sister, Carole Ann, dying young, her mother deserting her and father taking to the drink to drown his grief, she wanted to flee – the road trip across the country to see things she’d only read about in her precious books was going to be her way of grieving. Robinson would make it so much better - her nickname for him was Scalawag; he lived up to it daily with a mischievous smile to add to the tag.<br /><br />And so their journey began – before dawn one morning she snuck out of her apartment, leaving her dad asleep on the couch, and met Robinson near the bus depot. But they didn’t take the bus – the journey of a lifetime didn’t begin on a Greyhound bus said Robinson. As they roared off into the distance the exhilaration and excitement took Axi’s breathe away. It had begun…<br /><br />And so the two of them journeyed across the US, stopping here, camping there, sledding on sand dunes, using fake ID (they failed each time), eating Slim Jims (Robinson) and limp salad (Axi) to their heart’s content. They visited the Big Apple, LA, Detroit and everywhere in between. And all the time, Axi was trying to find the right time to declare her love for Robinson… And the future they didn’t want was edging closer…<br /><br />What a wonderful, sad, emotional and amazing story! It is a hugely difficult review to write as it would be sooo easy to give away spoilers. But the characters of sixteen year old Axi and seventeen year old Robinson are absolutely real. They form the basis of this story, they ARE the story, with many “along the way” characters who interweave throughout. The writing is beautiful – extremely poignant and moving. I have no hesitation in recommending this novel very highly.<br /><br />With thanks to NetGalley and the publisher for my copy to read and review.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15686059538788184424" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1133162737738052147"><b> "You have to remember the good stuff, Axi."<br/> ~Robinson~ </b><br/><br/>This book the second time round after 5 years....just pure wow! and the story and the encouragement given to one of the characters to just live life, love it, and enjoy the time you have here on earth.<br/><br/>When you learn by the halfway point once one of them (won't say who) coughs up blood, then you learn how the two met etc, that's when Patterson goes on this journey that I guess was a real eye opener for me in such a way. <br/><br/>There's a quote that </span>
  <span id="freeText1133162737738052147" style="display:none"><b> "You have to remember the good stuff, Axi."<br /> ~Robinson~ </b><br /><br />This book the second time round after 5 years....just pure wow! and the story and the encouragement given to one of the characters to just live life, love it, and enjoy the time you have here on earth.<br /><br />When you learn by the halfway point once one of them (won't say who) coughs up blood, then you learn how the two met etc, that's when Patterson goes on this journey that I guess was a real eye opener for me in such a way. <br /><br />There's a quote that says (not in the book) that I love which says, "Life is to be ENJOYED and not just to be endured" and it's so true and just like Axi and Robinson in this book, they did just that. <div id="review_854403974" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/854403974" />
    <a title="Leonel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4897732-leonel"><img alt="Leonel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296366047p2/4897732.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

  <span id="freeText12855848241231191448" style="display:none">Doesn't James Patterson write mysteries, or he is just known for them? Anyway, he wrote "First Love" with Emily Raymond. (But look at the typeface of both their names, and you can see who is marketed more) Maybe that's why this book is kind of a mess: it's muddled, unfocused and kind of dumb. Yes, I know it is about teenagers, and they may be the target market, but I thought the book felt dumbed-down. And I wish the characters were more likeable. Halfway through the book, I stopped caring about the characters even if the authors manipulate you into liking them. I cannot help but think that the book is a poor copy of John Green's "The Fault In Our Stars," so if you haven't read that yet, go grab that book instead because this one more or less tread the same road, and Green's book is infinitely better. <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://luhathoughts.blogspot.com/2014/02/ignore-this-love-book-review-first-love.html">http://luhathoughts.blogspot.com/2014...</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5808430087288053824">First Love really felt like a much inferior version of The Fault in Our Stars.   <span id="freeText5808430087288053824" style="display:none">First Love really felt like a much inferior version of The Fault in Our Stars. Really if you want to depress yourself by reading about young love and dying at least read John Green's poetic description and character building. I'm afraid James Patterson doesn't come close and he gives no moral uplift to couter the tragedy. Young love and living life to its fullest is great in theory, but a spontaneous cross country trip can still be exciting without breaking laws. I don't care who is dying, stealing cars and joy riding should not be glorified. The characters were likable, but there is nothing about this that I can recommend to any fellow readers.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer996939884&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer996939884" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17708664320416791401">1. I hated this book. Hated. I didn't cry. I didn't feel any emotion when Robinson died. Everything was annoying to me.<br/>2. Annoying things: the characters trying to sound smart but then explaining the vocabulary words or book references which made the reader feel annoyed because it assumes that the reader doesn't know anything. The use of the words gobsmacked and scalawag too many times. The lack of emotion I felt for anything in this book. That Robinson left his family for Axi and never did anyt</span>
  <span id="freeText17708664320416791401" style="display:none">1. I hated this book. Hated. I didn't cry. I didn't feel any emotion when Robinson died. Everything was annoying to me.<br />2. Annoying things: the characters trying to sound smart but then explaining the vocabulary words or book references which made the reader feel annoyed because it assumes that the reader doesn't know anything. The use of the words gobsmacked and scalawag too many times. The lack of emotion I felt for anything in this book. That Robinson left his family for Axi and never did anything about it until the road trip. Who leaves an amazing family behind when they have cancer? That Axi turned herself in. It was just stupid. How the frick could two minors go into a hospital without ID, insurance, parents. And also there's no way the amount of money they had could have covered the trip. That basically this was a knock off of The Fault in Our Stars.<br />3. Things in common with The Fault in Our Stars: they both have cancer. The characters are sort of quippy and sarcastic. They make references to the stars. They have a big adventure that helps them with their love story and find themselves. There's a sex scene. The boy dies.<br />4. The only reason I kept reading was to find out how it ended. If this wasn't a library book I probably would have ripped the pages out one by one, shredded them, and not composted them. Because this book wasn't even worthy of helping make good dirt. I would have thrown the shreds away, let it go to a landfill, and hoped that it landed by poopy toilet paper or a used diaper.<br />5. I'm throwing up in my mouth. I want to punch the characters. I want to get the time back in my my life that it took to read this.</span>

  <span id="freeText3245214750369731491" style="display:none">My first James Patterson! This reminded me a lot of The Fault in our stars crossed with Nick and Norah's infinite playlist. <br /><br />James Patterson, you can tell - is a master storyteller. Bah, it's me James, not you. <br /><br />This was such a nice refresher from all the love stories that I have been reading lately. I am definitely adding more Patterson to my book shelf!   <span id="freeText4619637184139479905" style="display:none">Sigh. I'm not sure how to review this book, so here is my ramble. This book started out adorable and young adult-ish. The familiar good girl with a crush on her best friend that could charm an angry wasp with a crooked smile. Then somewhere around page 100 it became something else, sort of outlandish and Bonnie &amp; Clyde. Then suddenly it was 'The Fault in Our Stars'. And even though you knew how it would end, it still gets you to sob at the end. Not what I initially expected. I think because the cover is kind of lame. I hope the paperback has a better cover so that it appeals to more people, although the fact that James Patterson wrote it is kind of a given. :)</span>

  <span id="freeText11072473468551166785" style="display:none">Two best friends decide to run away on a cross-country trip that turns into a Bonnie &amp; Clyde type adventure. Along the way, Axi and Robinson finally admit they have feelings for each other and curse themselves for waiting so long to admit it, especially when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ it becomes obvious that time is short for one of them.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />At first, I was wondering what the heck I was reading when their somewhat innocent trip to see the country turns quickly to one of crime. I thought they were good kids that just wanted to escape a little high school stress by seeing the world. I didn't expect their quest for adventure to be quite so risky and was shocked with they stole their first vehicle, but then we find out that life has dealt them both a pretty shitty hand and it starts to make sense. I really felt for Axi and Robinson and even cried a little at the end. </span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316207041" href="/book/show/17899371-first-love">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3541711-thepromoparrot?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer822120204" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10991676917745072875">In a story that is remarkably inspiring, poignant, memorable and full of adventure, James Patterson, the bestselling author of the Alex Cross thrillers and The Women's Murder Club series, has taken a leap into a world of romance with his new novel, First Love, in partnership with Emily Raymond. For those who have identified him with his brand of heart-pounding, out-of-this-world thrillers, the switch is like having a bad dream. But once you get into the story, you'll understand why James Patters</span>
  <span id="freeText10991676917745072875" style="display:none">In a story that is remarkably inspiring, poignant, memorable and full of adventure, James Patterson, the bestselling author of the Alex Cross thrillers and The Women's Murder Club series, has taken a leap into a world of romance with his new novel, First Love, in partnership with Emily Raymond. For those who have identified him with his brand of heart-pounding, out-of-this-world thrillers, the switch is like having a bad dream. But once you get into the story, you'll understand why James Patterson has to tell this tale.<br /><br />Axi Moore is a 'good girl' who comes from a family ravaged by tragedy. Her normal world was turned upside-down with the death of her sister from an incurable cancer. She was also diagnosed with cancer. Unable to cope with the situation, her mother ran away, never to be seen again. Her heart-broken father takes to drinking, to escape reality. It's a family devastated by tragedy in every conceivable way.<br /><br />But a flicker of hope inside her keeps burning. A chance encounter with another cancer patient, Oscar James Robinson, changes her life for the second time. She's plain crazy about him. Axi decides to go on an impulsive cross-country road-trip, and asks Robinson to accompany her. It's a dream come true for both of them. Axi and Robinson cherish the time they are sharing together, with Axi taking snapshots of their adventure which are spread all over the book. But their happiness is short-lived as the carefree adventure soon spins out of control. Will Axi and Robinson survive the ordeal? What has life in store for them?<br /><br />First Love by James Patterson is a beautiful and heart-rending journey of laughter and tears as Axi and Robinson face the greatest test of life - life itself. Sometimes life will take a turn that you would never anticipate. A truly great contemporary romance, it's difficult to sum up in words the emotions you feel about it. The knowledge that it's partly based on the author's life makes it even more evocative and heartfelt. For fans of James Patterson's brand of thrillers, it's time to take a break and explore the romantic side of the author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10991676917745072875" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1731282927647274969">I absolutely love James Patterson's writing and this book didn't disappoint. I read some of the reviews and people compared this to fault in our stars & pretty much said this was a copycat. I personally didn't think so and felt this one had more of an adventure to it and was an entirely new plot line and it got to the point. It was a sweet love story and got me back into reading more.   <span id="freeText1731282927647274969" style="display:none">I absolutely love James Patterson's writing and this book didn't disappoint. I read some of the reviews and people compared this to fault in our stars &amp; pretty much said this was a copycat. I personally didn't think so and felt this one had more of an adventure to it and was an entirely new plot line and it got to the point. It was a sweet love story and got me back into reading more. I'm glad it was more of a short story and the ending was predictable but sad.<br><b> The Good </b><br>It was fast paced and a short book you can get into. I loved the setting and I needed a cute romance story to get me through the beginning of August even though the ending wasn't all that happy. <br><b> The Bad </b> <br>You can predict what's going to happen in the story because how far can a pair of teenagers make it? Especially with the way they started.<br><b> Overall </b> <br>I would recommend this book for sure because let us be honest when does James Patterson ever write a bad book??? <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465577812ra/19376259.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1051904379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8258060221348945587">Patterson pens another of his lighter novels with some personal experiences to fuel the plot. When good girl Axi convinces her best friend, Robinson, to take a road trip, he gladly obliges. More than bad boy, Robinson studies her map and off they head, forging new and exciting trails along the way. While Axi experiences the thrill of stealing cars and sleeping on roadsides, she begins to admit to herself and the reader that her love for Robinson has been long brewing, but her cowardice has kept </span>
  <span id="freeText8258060221348945587" style="display:none">Patterson pens another of his lighter novels with some personal experiences to fuel the plot. When good girl Axi convinces her best friend, Robinson, to take a road trip, he gladly obliges. More than bad boy, Robinson studies her map and off they head, forging new and exciting trails along the way. While Axi experiences the thrill of stealing cars and sleeping on roadsides, she begins to admit to herself and the reader that her love for Robinson has been long brewing, but her cowardice has kept her from admitting it. After a medical emergency halts their trip, Axi and Robinson begin to see one another in a new light, or perhaps one that they have simply sheltered from one another. In an effort to complete their promised trip, they break more rules and head out, now fully inebriated in their emotions. Patterson sucks the reader in by this point, only to leave the most emotional (and somewhat predictable) segment of the story for last, as Axi's emotions and her delay in expressing them may come back to haunt her. Turning off his aggressive side, Patterson returns with a novel that warms the deepest part of the heart and leaves a tear embedded in the reader's eye, as young love flourishes.<br /><br />As I am in the middle of reading three Patterson novels, all from different genres and/or series, I have come to see the author in a few lights. I cannot discount that since he chooses to play the co-author card with most of his books, he will likely flavour each novel differently. That said, it still bears mentioning that this novel, a stand-alone, soars well above some of his other work, even those one-off mysteries he has penned in the last five years. While I am not out of touch with my emotional side, I have always preferred a crime or thriller to something heart-wrenching or romantically inclined. That said, in my long Patterson reading recollection, none of those sappy books he has put his name to have been poorly crafted. This novel is equally as powerful in its emotional impact and development, taking teenagers as the two long-loving characters. Patterson makes the story seem realistic, even if it is knowingly a tad hokey. Perhaps seeking to capture an oft-forgotten reader in his usual genre, Patterson presents a sappy love story to show that he can switch gears. He does so effectively and with little slaughtering of the intended emotional output.<br /><br />Kudos, Mr. Patterson on this novel. If only many of your other co-authored pieces could flow as nicely and not simply be a way for you to line your pockets while you produce drivel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8258060221348945587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_850670033" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/850670033" />
    <a title="Anjz Baccay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23411395-anjz-baccay"><img alt="Anjz Baccay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384336879p2/23411395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/850670033?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anjz Baccay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anjz Baccay" href="/user/show/23411395-anjz-baccay">Anjz Baccay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer850670033" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11971837887258381997"> First love is an adventure. It is about two people in search of the spices and thrills of life. Axi may not know it but what she is really looking for is hope and Robinson, life. Axi has a complicated family and that would make one think that that is her reason of her escaping town. This may lead readers to think <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ that this journey focuses on Axi, but actually it is about Robinson.  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/> [It was actually fun reading it especially on the first parts. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ The</span></span>
  <span id="freeText11971837887258381997" style="display:none"> First love is an adventure. It is about two people in search of the spices and thrills of life. Axi may not know it but what she is really looking for is hope and Robinson, life. Axi has a complicated family and that would make one think that that is her reason of her escaping town. This may lead readers to think <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ that this journey focuses on Axi, but actually it is about Robinson.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /> [It was actually fun reading it especially on the first parts. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The moments where Axi gets her hopes up of Robinson confessing to her when he really is talking about completely different things. Talk about being in the friend zone. It's funny when Axi gets flustered over them. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> She's also funny when she admits (to herself only) what she's honestly thinking at the moment, especially matters about Robinson.]<br /><br /> It was an epic battle with life and love. I think these two people were brought together by destiny. They are meant for each other. I almost cried in the end but the last and most important scene wasn't really agonizingly presented and not really sadistic. And it was just right. It felt like the unfair and right ending for me, however contrasting that sounds.<br /><br /> The narration was good. You could tell that James Patterson wrote it from the heart. I quote this from the book's overview, "... A remarkably moving tale with its origins in James Patterson's own past, this novel is a testament to the power of fist love-and how it can change the rest of your life." This is completely true and that is what I really felt. This (kind of experience of James Patterson) is the kind that he could pass down to his grandchildren and their children's children. I felt very honored to be able to read and be shared to this powerful story even without being a part of their family.<br /><br /> I like Axi's character very much because we share some traits such as being a "good girl" and being a bookworm I like her personality along the trip and...I like her as a whole person. Robinson is a dependable person and is very easy to love. He was always there for Axi and Axi for him. Not only the love was great but also their friendship.<br /><br /> I'm glad that Axi's relationship with dad got okay already in the end (I assume).<br /><br /> This novel actually got me very interested about the real story of James Patterson and his first love.<br /><br /> This is one of the best romantic novel I've ever read yet.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11971837887258381997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_30201091'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30201091-hot-winter-nights"><img alt="Hot Winter Nights (Bear Mountain Rescue, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1475745103l/30201091._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xspXW9N0GZSTScajVN6aZ7zcy/VekriP7fwO8YpKFcAe1lLqDCV2a2z5gF9ynKv5vkdfJVTgDPQZYT+I4Q4gkw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

Mom doesn’t believe Travis’s story, but Grandma knows: she says dreamtime is just as real as awake time. Grandpa continues to visit Travis, sharing details about the different styles of play, the types of equipment, the various traditions among the tribes. Wearing his grandfather’s gear, Travis gains confidence as he practices with the team. When opportunity strikes at the big game, he carries the durable weight of tradition onto the field with him, celebrating skills handed down through generations.Co-owner of Redbird Media and Design, Art Coulson (Cherokee) is an award-winning writer and editor with decades of experience playing lacrosse. Robert DesJarlait (Anishinaabe, Red Lake), cofounder of Protect Our Manoomin, is an artist and activist who illustrated Meridel LeSueur’s Sparrow Hawk.<\/span>\n  <a <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4068121357570379357"><a href='http://www.jamespatterson.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Official US Site</a><br/><a href='http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk' rel='nofollow noopener'>Official UK Site</a><br/><a href='http://jimmypatterson.org' rel='nofollow noopener'>JIMMY Patterson Books</a><br/><a href='http://readkiddoread.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>ReadKiddoRead</a><br/><br/><br/><br/>James Patterson is the world’s bestselling author and most trusted storyteller. He has created more enduring fictional characters than any other novelist writing today, with his Alex Cross, Michael Bennett, Women’s Murder Club, Private, NYPD Red, Daniel X, Maximum Ride, and Middle School series. He has sold over 380 million books wo</span>
  <span id="freeText4068121357570379357" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.jamespatterson.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Official US Site</a><br /><a href="http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Official UK Site</a><br /><a href="http://jimmypatterson.org" rel="nofollow noopener">JIMMY Patterson Books</a><br /><a href="http://readkiddoread.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadKiddoRead</a><br /><br /><br /><br />James Patterson is the world’s bestselling author and most trusted storyteller. He has created more enduring fictional characters than any other novelist writing today, with his Alex Cross, Michael Bennett, Women’s Murder Club, Private, NYPD Red, Daniel X, Maximum Ride, and Middle School series. He has sold over 380 million books worldwide and currently holds the Guinness World Record for the most #1 New York Times bestsellers. In addition to writing the thriller novels for which he is best known, among them The President Is Missing with President Bill Clinton, Patterson also writes fiction for young readers of all ages, including the Max Einstein series, produced in partnership with the Albert Einstein Estate. He is also the first author to have #1 new titles simultaneously on the New York Times adult and children’s bestseller lists.<br /> <br />The son of an insurance salesman and a schoolteacher, Patterson grew up in Newburgh, New York, and began casually writing at the age of nineteen. In 1969, he graduated from Manhattan College. He was given a full-ride scholarship to Vanderbilt University’s graduate program in English. He left Vanderbilt before getting his PhD due to complications involving the Vietnam War. <br /> <br />Instead, he moved to New York to become a junior copywriter for the advertising agency J. Walter Thompson, eventually becoming CEO of its North American company.<br /> <br />In 1976, while still working for J. Walter Thompson, Patterson published his first novel, The Thomas Berryman Number, with Little, Brown and Company. After being turned down by thirty-one publishers, it won the Edgar Award for Best First Novel. Patterson’s 1993 novel, Along Came a Spider, his first book to feature Alex Cross, was also his first New York Times bestseller in fiction.<br /> <br />In 2001, Morgan Freeman starred as Alex Cross in a film adaptation of Along Came a Spider, and Tyler Perry also played the character in the 2012 film Alex Cross. A film adaptation of Patterson’s middle-grade novel Middle School: The Worst Years of My Life was released in theaters in October 2016.<br /> <br />James Patterson has donated more than one million books to students, focusing on some of the most under-resourced schools and youth programs in the country. To date, he has donated $7.25 million to school and classroom libraries throughout the United States, and $2.1 million to independent bookstores and employees.<br /> <br />Patterson has recently donated over $35 million to his and his wife’s alma maters—the University of Wisconsin, Vanderbilt University, and Manhattan College—and he has established over four hundred Teacher and Writer Education Scholarships at twenty-one colleges and universities throughout the country. Patterson has also donated more than one million books to U.S. soldiers at home and overseas.<br /> <br />In May 2015, Patterson launched a children’s book imprint at Little, Brown—JIMMY Patterson—that is unwaveringly focused on one goal: turning kids into lifelong readers. This imprint also provides resources, strategies, and programs to serve teachers, parents, librarians, and booksellers. Patterson invests proceeds from the sales of JIMMY Patterson Books in pro-reading initiatives.<br /> <br />Patterson also founded ReadKiddoRead.com, a website designed to help parents, teachers, and librarians ignite a new generation’s excitement for reading. Awarded the National Book Foundation’s Innovations in Reading Prize and the American Library Association’s Great Websites for Kids, the site features thoughtful book reviews from a variety of genres and age ranges, a large and lively Facebook community, and contributions from other authors.<br /> <br />Patterson’s awards for adult and children’s literature include the Edgar Award, the International </span>
  <a data-text-id="4068121357570379357" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
